<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Districts_and_enlargement">Districts and enlargement</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Vienna&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Districts and enlargement">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Districts_of_Vienna" title="Districts of Vienna">Districts of Vienna</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Vienna,_administrative_divisions_-_Nmbrs.svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1312" data-file-width="1669" height="173" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1f/Vienna%2C_administrative_divisions_-_Nmbrs.svg/220px-Vienna%2C_administrative_divisions_-_Nmbrs.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1f/Vienna%2C_administrative_divisions_-_Nmbrs.svg/330px-Vienna%2C_administrative_divisions_-_Nmbrs.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1f/Vienna%2C_administrative_divisions_-_Nmbrs.svg/440px-Vienna%2C_administrative_divisions_-_Nmbrs.svg.png 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Vienna,_administrative_divisions_-_Nmbrs.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Map of the districts of Vienna with numbers</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Vienna is composed of 23 districts (<i>Bezirke</i>). Administrative district offices in Vienna (called Magistratische Bezirksämter) serve functions similar to those in the other Austrian states (called Bezirkshauptmannschaften), the officers being subject to the mayor of Vienna; with the notable exception of the police, which is under federal supervision.</p>
<p>District residents in Vienna (Austrians as well as EU citizens with permanent residence here) elect a District Assembly (Bezirksvertretung). City hall has delegated maintenance budgets, e.g., for schools and parks, so that the districts are able to set priorities autonomously. Any decision of a district can be overridden by the city assembly (Gemeinderat) or the responsible city councillor (amtsführender Stadrat).</p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Opera-Vienna-Austria-2005.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1536" data-file-width="2048" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6b/Opera-Vienna-Austria-2005.jpg/220px-Opera-Vienna-Austria-2005.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6b/Opera-Vienna-Austria-2005.jpg/330px-Opera-Vienna-Austria-2005.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6b/Opera-Vienna-Austria-2005.jpg/440px-Opera-Vienna-Austria-2005.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Opera-Vienna-Austria-2005.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Albertina Terrace in the Innere Stadt</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Ringlinien08.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2736" data-file-width="3648" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7e/Ringlinien08.JPG/220px-Ringlinien08.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7e/Ringlinien08.JPG/330px-Ringlinien08.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7e/Ringlinien08.JPG/440px-Ringlinien08.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Ringlinien08.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The Ring Road (Ringstraße) with a historical tram</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The heart and historical city of Vienna, a large part of today's <a href="/wiki/Innere_Stadt" title="Innere Stadt">Innere Stadt</a>, was a fortress surrounded by fields in order to defend itself from potential attackers. In 1850, Vienna with the consent of the emperor annexed 34 surrounding villages,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-61"><a href="#cite_note-61">[61]</a></sup> called Vorstädte, into the city limits (districts no. 2 to 8, after 1861 with the separation of Margareten from Wieden no. 2 to 9). Consequently, the walls were razed after 1857,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-62"><a href="#cite_note-62">[62]</a></sup> making it possible for the city centre to expand.</p>
<p>In their place, a broad boulevard called the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ringstra%C3%9Fe" title="Ringstraße">Ringstraße</a> was built, along which imposing public and private buildings, monuments, and parks were created by the start of the 20th century. These buildings include the <a href="/wiki/Rathaus,_Vienna" title="Rathaus, Vienna">Rathaus</a> (town hall), the <a href="/wiki/Burgtheater" title="Burgtheater">Burgtheater</a>, the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Vienna" title="University of Vienna">University</a>, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Parliament_of_Austria" title="Parliament of Austria">Parliament</a>, the twin museums of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Naturhistorisches_Museum" title="Naturhistorisches Museum">natural history</a> and <a href="/wiki/Kunsthistorisches_Museum" title="Kunsthistorisches Museum">fine art</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Vienna_State_Opera" title="Vienna State Opera">Staatsoper</a>. It is also the location of New Wing of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hofburg_Imperial_Palace" title="Hofburg Imperial Palace">Hofburg</a>, the former imperial palace, and the Imperial and Royal War Ministry finished in 1913. The mainly <a href="/wiki/Gothic_architecture" title="Gothic architecture">Gothic</a> <a href="/wiki/St._Stephen%27s_Cathedral,_Vienna" title="St. Stephen's Cathedral, Vienna">Stephansdom</a> is located at the centre of the city, on <a href="/wiki/Stephansplatz,_Vienna" title="Stephansplatz, Vienna">Stephansplatz</a>. The Imperial-Royal Government set up the Vienna City Renovation Fund (Wiener Stadterneuerungsfonds) and sold many building lots to private investors, thereby partly financing public construction works.</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Urania_3904-Christian_Michelides.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2448" data-file-width="3264" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/04/Urania_3904-Christian_Michelides.jpg/220px-Urania_3904-Christian_Michelides.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/04/Urania_3904-Christian_Michelides.jpg/330px-Urania_3904-Christian_Michelides.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/04/Urania_3904-Christian_Michelides.jpg/440px-Urania_3904-Christian_Michelides.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Urania_3904-Christian_Michelides.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Urania_(Vienna)" title="Urania (Vienna)">Urania</a> at sunset</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Vienna_Skyline.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3264" data-file-width="4912" height="146" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e5/Vienna_Skyline.jpg/220px-Vienna_Skyline.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e5/Vienna_Skyline.jpg/330px-Vienna_Skyline.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e5/Vienna_Skyline.jpg/440px-Vienna_Skyline.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Vienna_Skyline.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Skyline of <a href="/wiki/Donaustadt" title="Donaustadt">Donaustadt</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>From 1850 to 1890, city limits in the West and the South mainly followed another wall called <i><a href="/wiki/Linienwall" title="Linienwall">Linienwall</a></i> at which a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Road_toll_(historic)" title="Road toll (historic)">road toll</a> called the <i><a href="/wiki/Liniengeld" title="Liniengeld">Liniengeld</a></i> was charged. Outside this wall from 1873 onwards a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Beltway" title="Beltway">ring road</a> called <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/G%C3%BCrtel,_Vienna" title="Gürtel, Vienna">Gürtel</a> was built. In 1890 it was decided to integrate 33 suburbs (called Vororte) beyond that wall into Vienna by 1 January 1892<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-vol5p290_63-0"><a href="#cite_note-vol5p290-63">[63]</a></sup> and transform them into districts no. 11 to 19 (district no. 10 had been constituted in 1874); hence the Linienwall was torn down beginning in 1894.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-64"><a href="#cite_note-64">[64]</a></sup> In 1900, district no. 20, Brigittenau, was created by separating the area from the 2nd district.</p>
<p>From 1850 to 1904, Vienna had expanded only on the right bank of the Danube, following the main branch before the regulation of 1868–1875, i.e., the Old Danube of today. In 1904, the 21st district was created by integrating Floridsdorf, Kagran, Stadlau, Hirschstetten, Aspern and other villages on the left bank of the Danube into Vienna, in 1910 Strebersdorf followed. On 15 October 1938 the Nazis created Great Vienna with 26 districts by merging 97 towns and villages into Vienna, 80 of which were returned to surrounding <a href="/wiki/Lower_Austria" title="Lower Austria">Lower Austria</a> in 1954.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-vol5p290_63-1"><a href="#cite_note-vol5p290-63">[63]</a></sup> Since then Vienna has 23 districts.</p>
<p>Industries are located mostly in the southern and eastern districts. The <a href="/wiki/Innere_Stadt" title="Innere Stadt">Innere Stadt</a> is situated away from the main flow of the <a href="/wiki/Danube" title="Danube">Danube</a>, but is bounded by the <i><a href="/wiki/Donaukanal" title="Donaukanal">Donaukanal</a></i> ("Danube canal"). Vienna's second and twentieth districts are located between the Donaukanal and the <a href="/wiki/Danube" title="Danube">Danube</a> River. Across the Danube, where the <a href="/wiki/Vienna_International_Centre" title="Vienna International Centre">Vienna International Centre</a> is located (districts 21–22), and in the southern areas (district 23) are the newest parts of the city.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Politics">Politics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Vienna&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Politics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Reichsrat_Vienna_Okt_2007_P2.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2168" data-file-width="2152" height="222" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/10/Reichsrat_Vienna_Okt_2007_P2.jpg/220px-Reichsrat_Vienna_Okt_2007_P2.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/10/Reichsrat_Vienna_Okt_2007_P2.jpg/330px-Reichsrat_Vienna_Okt_2007_P2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/10/Reichsrat_Vienna_Okt_2007_P2.jpg/440px-Reichsrat_Vienna_Okt_2007_P2.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Reichsrat_Vienna_Okt_2007_P2.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Austrian_Parliament_Building" title="Austrian Parliament Building">Austrian Parliament Buildings</a> Debating Chamber of the former House of Deputies of Austria</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Parlament_-_B%C3%A9cs,_2014.12.03_(39).JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3232" data-file-width="3232" height="220" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/87/Parlament_-_B%C3%A9cs%2C_2014.12.03_%2839%29.JPG/220px-Parlament_-_B%C3%A9cs%2C_2014.12.03_%2839%29.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/87/Parlament_-_B%C3%A9cs%2C_2014.12.03_%2839%29.JPG/330px-Parlament_-_B%C3%A9cs%2C_2014.12.03_%2839%29.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/87/Parlament_-_B%C3%A9cs%2C_2014.12.03_%2839%29.JPG/440px-Parlament_-_B%C3%A9cs%2C_2014.12.03_%2839%29.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Parlament_-_B%C3%A9cs,_2014.12.03_(39).JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
House of Deputies</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In the twenty years before the First World War and until 1918, Viennese politics were shaped by the <a href="/wiki/Christian_Social_Party_(Austria)" title="Christian Social Party (Austria)">Christian Social Party</a>, in particular long-term mayor <a href="/wiki/Karl_Lueger" title="Karl Lueger">Karl Lueger</a>; he managed not to apply the general voting rights for men introduced by and for the parliament of imperial Austria, the <i>Reichsrat</i>, in 1907, thereby excluding most of the working class from taking part in decisions. For <a href="/wiki/Adolf_Hitler" title="Adolf Hitler">Adolf Hitler</a>, who spent some years in Vienna, Lueger was a remarkable teacher of how to use <a href="/wiki/Antisemitism" title="Antisemitism">antisemitism</a> in politics.</p>
<p>Vienna is today considered the centre of the <a href="/wiki/Social_Democratic_Party_of_Austria" title="Social Democratic Party of Austria">Social Democratic Party</a>. During the period of the <a href="/wiki/Federal_State_of_Austria" title="Federal State of Austria">First Republic</a> (1918–1934), the Vienna <a href="/wiki/Social_democracy" title="Social democracy">Social Democrats</a> undertook many overdue social reforms. At that time, Vienna's municipal policy was admired by Socialists throughout Europe, who therefore referred to the city as "<a href="/wiki/Red_Vienna" title="Red Vienna">Red Vienna</a>" (<i>Rotes Wien</i>). In February 1934 troops of the Austrian federal government under <a href="/wiki/Engelbert_Dollfuss" title="Engelbert Dollfuss">Engelbert Dollfuss</a>, who had closed down the first chamber of the federal parliament, the <i>Nationalrat</i>, in 1933, and paramilitary socialist organisations were engaged in the Austrian civil war, which led to the ban of the Social Democratic party.</p>
<p>For most of the time since after the First World War, the city has been governed by the <a href="/wiki/Social_Democratic_Party_of_Austria" title="Social Democratic Party of Austria">Social Democratic Party</a> (SPÖ) with absolute majorities in the city parliament. Only between 1934 and 1945, when the Social Democratic Party was illegal, mayors were appointed by the <a href="/wiki/Austrofascism" title="Austrofascism">austro-fascist</a> and later by the <a href="/wiki/Nazi_Party" title="Nazi Party">Nazi</a> authorities. The current mayor of Vienna is <a href="/wiki/Michael_H%C3%A4upl" title="Michael Häupl">Michael Häupl</a> of the SPÖ. As rural Austria is dominated by conservative citizens, if the Social Democrats would not maintain their nearly unbreakable hold on Vienna, the rival <a href="/wiki/Austrian_People%27s_Party" title="Austrian People's Party">Austrian People's Party</a> (ÖVP) would dominate Austrian politics.</p>
<p>The city has enacted many social democratic policies. The <i><a href="/wiki/Gemeindebau" title="Gemeindebau">Gemeindebauten</a></i> are social housing assets that are well integrated into the city architecture outside the first or "inner" district. The low rents enable comfortable accommodation and good access to the city amenities. Many of the projects were built after <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a> on vacant lots that were destroyed by bombing during the war. The city took particular pride in building them to a high standard.</p>
<p>Since Vienna obtained federal state (<i>Bundesland</i>) status of its own by the federal constitution of 1920, the mayor (except 1934–1945) also holds the function of the state governor (<i>Landeshauptmann</i>). The Rathaus accommodates the offices of the mayor (<i>Magistrat der Stadt Wien</i>) and the state government (<i>Landesregierung</i>). The city is administered by a multitude of departments (<i>Magistratsabteilungen</i>), politically supervised by <i>amtsführende Stadträte</i> (members of the city government leading offices; according to the Vienna constitution opposition parties have the right to designate members of the city government not leading offices).</p>
<p>In the 1996 City Council election, the SPÖ lost its overall majority in the 100-seat chamber, winning 43 seats and 39.15% of the vote. In 1996 the <a href="/wiki/Freedom_Party_of_Austria" title="Freedom Party of Austria">Freedom Party of Austria</a> (FPÖ), which won 29 seats (up from 21 in 1991), beat the ÖVP into third place for the second time running. From 1996–2001, the SPÖ governed Vienna in a coalition with the ÖVP. In 2001 the SPÖ regained the overall majority with 52 seats and 46.91% of the vote; in October 2005 this majority was increased further to 55 seats (49.09%). In course of the 2010 city council elections the SPÖ lost their overall majority again and consequently forged a coalition with the <a href="/wiki/The_Greens_%E2%80%93_The_Green_Alternative" title="The Greens – The Green Alternative">Green Party</a> – the first SPÖ/Green coalition in Austria.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-65"><a href="#cite_note-65">[65]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Vienna&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Economy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:13-08-30-wien-by-RalfR-123.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2848" data-file-width="4288" height="146" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e9/13-08-30-wien-by-RalfR-123.jpg/220px-13-08-30-wien-by-RalfR-123.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e9/13-08-30-wien-by-RalfR-123.jpg/330px-13-08-30-wien-by-RalfR-123.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e9/13-08-30-wien-by-RalfR-123.jpg/440px-13-08-30-wien-by-RalfR-123.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:13-08-30-wien-by-RalfR-123.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/High-rise" title="High-rise">High-rise</a> buildings in the outer district</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Messe_Wien_01.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1688" data-file-width="3000" height="124" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8b/Messe_Wien_01.jpg/220px-Messe_Wien_01.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8b/Messe_Wien_01.jpg/330px-Messe_Wien_01.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8b/Messe_Wien_01.jpg/440px-Messe_Wien_01.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Messe_Wien_01.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Messe Wien Congress Center</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Wien_-_Austria_Center.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1114" data-file-width="1575" height="156" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/52/Wien_-_Austria_Center.JPG/220px-Wien_-_Austria_Center.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/52/Wien_-_Austria_Center.JPG/330px-Wien_-_Austria_Center.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/52/Wien_-_Austria_Center.JPG/440px-Wien_-_Austria_Center.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Wien_-_Austria_Center.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Austria Center Vienna (ACV)</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Vienna is one of the wealthiest regions in the European Union: Its gross regional product of EUR 47,200 per capita constituted 25.7% of Austria's GDP in 2013. It amounts to 159% of the EU average.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-66"><a href="#cite_note-66">[66]</a></sup> The city improved its position from 2012 on the ranking of the most economically powerful cities reaching number nine on the listing in 2015.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-67"><a href="#cite_note-67">[67]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-68"><a href="#cite_note-68">[68]</a></sup></p>
<p>With a share of 85.5% in gross value added, the service sector is Vienna’s most important economic sector. Industry and commerce have a share of 14.5% in gross value added, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Primary_sector" title="Primary sector">primary sector</a> (agriculture) has a share of 0.07% and therefore plays a minor role in the local added value.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_69-0"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-69">[69]</a></sup> However, the cultivation and production of <a href="/wiki/Wine" title="Wine">wines</a> within the city borders have a high socio-cultural value. The most important business sectors are trade (14.7% of added value in Vienna), scientific and technological services, real estate and housing activities as well as manufacturing of goods. In 2012, Vienna’s contribution in Austria’s outgoing and incoming <a href="/wiki/Foreign_direct_investment" title="Foreign direct investment">foreign direct investments</a> was of about 60%, which demonstrates Vienna’s role as an international hub for domestic and foreign companies.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_69-1"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-69">[69]</a></sup></p>
<p>Since the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fall_of_the_Iron_Curtain" title="Fall of the Iron Curtain">fall of the Iron Curtain</a> in 1989, Vienna has expanded its position as gateway to Eastern Europe: 300 international companies have their Eastern European headquarters in Vienna and its environs. Among them are <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hewlett_Packard" title="Hewlett Packard">Hewlett Packard</a>, <a href="/wiki/Henkel" title="Henkel">Henkel</a>, <a href="/wiki/Baxalta" title="Baxalta">Baxalta</a> and <a href="/wiki/Siemens" title="Siemens">Siemens</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-70"><a href="#cite_note-70">[70]</a></sup> Companies in Vienna have extensive contacts and competences in business with Eastern Europe due to the city’s historical role as centre of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Habsburg_Empire" title="Habsburg Empire">Habsburg Empire</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-71"><a href="#cite_note-71">[71]</a></sup> The number of international businesses in Vienna is still growing: In 2014 159 and in 2015 175 international firms established offices in Vienna.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-72"><a href="#cite_note-72">[72]</a></sup></p>
<p>Altogether, approximately 8,300 new companies have been founded in Vienna every year since 2004.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-73"><a href="#cite_note-73">[73]</a></sup> The majority of these companies are operating in fields of industry-oriented services, wholesale trade as well as information and communications technologies and new media.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-74"><a href="#cite_note-74">[74]</a></sup> Vienna makes effort to establish itself as a start-up hub. Since 2012, the city hosts the annual <a class="external text" href="http://pioneers.io/festival2015/" rel="nofollow">Pioneers Festival</a>, the largest start-up event in Central Europe with 2,500 international participants taking place at <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hofburg_Palace" title="Hofburg Palace">Hofburg Palace</a>. <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Tech_Cocktail&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Tech Cocktail (page does not exist)">Tech Cocktail</a>, an online portal for the start-up scene, has ranked Vienna sixth among the top ten start-up cities worldwide.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-75"><a href="#cite_note-75">[75]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-76"><a href="#cite_note-76">[76]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-77"><a href="#cite_note-77">[77]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Research_and_development">Research and development</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Vienna&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Research and development">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The city of Vienna attaches major importance to science and research and focuses on creating a positive environment for research and development. In 2014, Vienna has accommodated 1,329 research facilities; 40,400 persons are employed in the R&amp;D sector and 35% of Austria’s R&amp;D expenses are invested in the city. With a research quota of 3.4% Vienna exceeds the Austrian average of 2.77% and has already met the EU target of 3.0% by 2020.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_69-2"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-69">[69]</a></sup> A major R&amp;D sector in Vienna are life sciences with 378 biotech, pharma and medtech companies such as <a href="/wiki/Johnson_%26_Johnson" title="Johnson &amp; Johnson">Johnson &amp; Johnson</a>, <a href="/wiki/Siemens" title="Siemens">Siemens</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hoffmann-La_Roche" title="Hoffmann-La Roche">Roche</a>, <a href="/wiki/Philips" title="Philips">Philips</a> and <a href="/wiki/Boehringer_Ingelheim" title="Boehringer Ingelheim">Boehringer Ingelheim</a>, with more than 21,000 employees. There are 25 public and private research institutions, among them the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Natural_Resources_and_Life_Sciences,_Vienna" title="University of Natural Resources and Life Sciences, Vienna">University of Natural Resources and Life Sciences (BOKU)</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Austrian_Institute_of_Technology" title="Austrian Institute of Technology">Austrian Institute of Technology</a> and the <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Campus_Vienna_Biocenter&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Campus Vienna Biocenter (page does not exist)">Campus Vienna Biocenter</a><span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;"> (<a class="extiw" href="https://de.wikipedia.org/wiki/Campus_Vienna_Biocenter" title="de:Campus Vienna Biocenter">de</a>)</span>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-78"><a href="#cite_note-78">[78]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Information_technologies">Information technologies</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Vienna&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Information technologies">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The Viennese sector for information and communication technologies is comparable in size with the sector in <a href="/wiki/Helsinki" title="Helsinki">Helsinki</a> or <a href="/wiki/Munich" title="Munich">Munich</a> and thus among Europe’s largest IT locations. In 2012 8,962 IT businesses with a workforce of 64,223 were located in the Vienna Region. The main products are instruments and appliances for measuring, testing and navigation as well as electronic components. More than ⅔ of the enterprises provide IT services. Among the biggest IT firms in Vienna are <a href="/wiki/Kapsch" title="Kapsch">Kapsch</a>, <a href="/wiki/Beko" title="Beko">Beko</a> Engineering &amp; Informatics, air trafﬁc control experts <a href="/wiki/Frequentis" title="Frequentis">Frequentis</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cisco_Systems" title="Cisco Systems">Cisco Systems</a> Austria, <a href="/wiki/Hewlett-Packard" title="Hewlett-Packard">Hewlett-Packard</a>, <a href="/wiki/Microsoft" title="Microsoft">Microsoft</a> Austria, <a href="/wiki/IBM" title="IBM">IBM</a> Austria and <a href="/wiki/Samsung_Electronics" title="Samsung Electronics">Samsung Electronics</a> Austria.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-administration1_79-0"><a href="#cite_note-administration1-79">[79]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-auto_80-0"><a href="#cite_note-auto-80">[80]</a></sup></p>
<p>The US technology corporation <a href="/wiki/Cisco_Systems" title="Cisco Systems">Cisco</a> runs its <i>Entrepreneurs in Residence</i> program for Europe in Vienna in cooperation with the <a class="external text" href="https://viennabusinessagency.at/about-us/the-company/organisation/" rel="nofollow">Vienna Business Agency</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-81"><a href="#cite_note-81">[81]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-82"><a href="#cite_note-82">[82]</a></sup></p>
<p>The British company <a href="/wiki/UBM_plc" title="UBM plc">UBM</a> has rated Vienna one of the <i>Top 10 Internet Cities</i> worldwide, by analysing criteria like connection speed, WIFI availability, innovation spirit and open government data.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-83"><a href="#cite_note-83">[83]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 2011 74.3% of Viennese households were connected with broadband, 79% were in possession of a computer. According to the broadband strategy of the City, full broadband coverage will be reached by 2020.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-administration1_79-1"><a href="#cite_note-administration1-79">[79]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-auto_80-1"><a href="#cite_note-auto-80">[80]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tourism_and_conferences">Tourism and conferences</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Vienna&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Tourism and conferences">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>6.2 million tourists visited Vienna in 2014 amounting to 13,524,266 overnight stays. The main markets for tourists are <a href="/wiki/Germany" title="Germany">Germany</a>, the <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a>, <a href="/wiki/Italy" title="Italy">Italy</a> and <a href="/wiki/Russia" title="Russia">Russia</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-84"><a href="#cite_note-84">[84]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-85"><a href="#cite_note-85">[85]</a></sup> Between 2005 and 2013, Vienna was the world's number one destination for international congresses and conventions. In 2014, 202 international conferences were held in Vienna, making it the second most popular congress location worldwide according to the statistics of the <a href="/wiki/International_Congress_and_Convention_Association" title="International Congress and Convention Association">International Congress and Convention Association</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-86"><a href="#cite_note-86">[86]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-87"><a href="#cite_note-87">[87]</a></sup> Its largest conference centre, the <a class="external text" href="https://www.acv.at/index.en.html" rel="nofollow">Austria Center Vienna (ACV)</a> has a total capacity for around 20,000 people and is situated next to the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Office_at_Vienna" title="United Nations Office at Vienna">United Nations Headquarters in Vienna</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-88"><a href="#cite_note-88">[88]</a></sup> Other centres are the <a class="external text" href="http://www.messe.at/en/index.html" rel="nofollow">Messe Wien Exhibition &amp; Congress Center</a> (up to 3,300 people) and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hofburg_Palace" title="Hofburg Palace">Hofburg Palace</a> (up to 4,900 people).</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Rankings">Rankings</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Vienna&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Rankings">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Regarding life quality, Vienna leads the <i>2016 Quality of Living Ranking</i> by the international <a href="/wiki/Mercer_(consulting_firm)" title="Mercer (consulting firm)">Mercer Consulting Group</a> for the seventh consecutive year.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-89"><a href="#cite_note-89">[89]</a></sup> In the 2015 liveability report by the Economist Intellicence Unit as well as in the <i>Quality of Life Survey 2015</i> of London-based <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Monocle_(media_company)" title="Monocle (media company)"><i>Monocle magazine</i></a> Vienna was equally ranked second most liveable city worldwide.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-90"><a href="#cite_note-90">[90]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-91"><a href="#cite_note-91">[91]</a></sup></p>
<p><a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Human_Settlements_Programme" title="United Nations Human Settlements Programme">The United Nations Human Settlements Programme <i>UN-Habitat</i></a> has ranked Vienna the most prosperous city in the world in its flagship report <i>State of the World Cities 2012/2013</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-92"><a href="#cite_note-92">[92]</a></sup></p>
<p>According to the 2014 <a class="external text" href="http://www.reputationinstitute.com/thought-leadership/city-reptrak" rel="nofollow">City RepTrack</a> ranking by the Reputation Institute, Vienna has the best reputation in comparison with 100 major global cities.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-93"><a href="#cite_note-93">[93]</a></sup></p>
<p>The <i>Innovation Cities Global Index 2014</i> by the Australian innovation agency <a class="external text" href="http://www.2thinknow.com/" rel="nofollow">2thinknow</a> ranks Vienna sixth behind <a href="/wiki/San_Francisco" title="San Francisco">San Francisco</a>-<a href="/wiki/San_Jose,_California" title="San Jose, California">San Jose</a>, <a href="/wiki/New_York_City" title="New York City">New York City</a>, <a href="/wiki/London" title="London">London</a>, <a href="/wiki/Boston" title="Boston">Boston</a> and <a href="/wiki/Paris" title="Paris">Paris</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-94"><a href="#cite_note-94">[94]</a></sup></p>
<p>US climate strategist <a href="/wiki/Boyd_Cohen" title="Boyd Cohen">Boyd Cohen</a> placed Vienna first in his first <i>global smart cities</i> ranking of 2012. In the 2014 ranking, Vienna reached third place among European cities behind <a href="/wiki/Copenhagen" title="Copenhagen">Copenhagen</a> and <a href="/wiki/Amsterdam" title="Amsterdam">Amsterdam</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-95"><a href="#cite_note-95">[95]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Urban_development">Urban development</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Vienna&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Urban development">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Central_Railway_Station">Central Railway Station</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Vienna&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Central Railway Station">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Vienna’s new <a href="/wiki/Wien_Hauptbahnhof" title="Wien Hauptbahnhof">Central Railway Station</a> was opened in October 2014.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-96"><a href="#cite_note-96">[96]</a></sup> Construction began in June 2007 and was due to last until December 2015. The station is served by 1,100 trains with 145,000 passengers. There is a shopping center with approximately 90 shops and restaurants. In the vicinity of the station a new district is emerging with 550,000 m<sup>2</sup> (5,920,000 sq ft) office space and 5,000 apartments until 2020.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-97"><a href="#cite_note-97">[97]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-98"><a href="#cite_note-98">[98]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-99"><a href="#cite_note-99">[99]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Aspern">Aspern</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Vienna&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Aspern">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Seestadt Aspern is one of the largest urban expansion projects of Europe. A 5 <a href="/wiki/Hectare" title="Hectare">hectare</a> artificial lake, offices, apartments and a tube station within walking distance are supposed to attract 20,000 new citizens when construction is completed in 2028.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-100"><a href="#cite_note-100">[100]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-101"><a href="#cite_note-101">[101]</a></sup> In addition, the highest wooden skyscraper of the world called “HoHo Wien” will be built within 3 years, starting in 2015.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-102"><a href="#cite_note-102">[102]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Smart_City">Smart City</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Vienna&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Smart City">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In 2014, the Vienna City Council adopted the Smart City Wien Framework Strategy 2050. It is a long-term umbrella strategy that is supposed to establish a conducive, long-term and structural framework in order to reduce carbon dioxide emissions from 3.1 tonnes per capita to 1 tonne per capita by 2050, have 50% of Vienna’s gross energy consumption <a href="/wiki/Renewable_energy" title="Renewable energy">originate from renewable sources</a> and to reduce motorized individual traffic from the current 28% to 15% by 2030. A stated goal is that, by 2050, all vehicles within the municipal boundaries will run without conventional propulsion technologies. Additionally, Vienna aims to be one of the five biggest European research and innovation hubs in 2050.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-103"><a href="#cite_note-103">[103]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Religion">Religion</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Vienna&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Religion">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Karlskirche,_Vienna.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2336" data-file-width="3504" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7b/Karlskirche%2C_Vienna.jpg/220px-Karlskirche%2C_Vienna.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7b/Karlskirche%2C_Vienna.jpg/330px-Karlskirche%2C_Vienna.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7b/Karlskirche%2C_Vienna.jpg/440px-Karlskirche%2C_Vienna.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Karlskirche,_Vienna.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Karlskirche" title="Karlskirche">Karlskirche</a>, Vienna</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Advent_in_Wien_-_2014.12.03_(44).JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3240" data-file-width="4320" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/34/Advent_in_Wien_-_2014.12.03_%2844%29.JPG/220px-Advent_in_Wien_-_2014.12.03_%2844%29.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/34/Advent_in_Wien_-_2014.12.03_%2844%29.JPG/330px-Advent_in_Wien_-_2014.12.03_%2844%29.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/34/Advent_in_Wien_-_2014.12.03_%2844%29.JPG/440px-Advent_in_Wien_-_2014.12.03_%2844%29.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Advent_in_Wien_-_2014.12.03_(44).JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Stephansdom</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>According to the 2001 census, 49.2% of Viennese were Roman Catholics, while 25.7% were of no religion, 7.8% were Muslim, 6.0% were members of an Orthodox denomination, 4.7% were Protestant (mostly Lutheran), 0.5% were Jewish and 6.3% were either of other religions or did not reply.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-census_57-1"><a href="#cite_note-census-57">[57]</a></sup> By 2011 the shares of religious bodies had significantly changed:<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-104"><a href="#cite_note-104">[104]</a></sup></p>
<ul>
<li>41.3% Catholics</li>
<li>31.6% no religion</li>
<li>11.6% Muslim</li>
<li>8.4% Orthodox</li>
<li>4.2% Protestant</li>
<li>2.9% others</li>
</ul>
<p>Vienna is the seat of the Metropolitan <a href="/wiki/Roman_Catholic_Archdiocese_of_Vienna" title="Roman Catholic Archdiocese of Vienna">Roman Catholic Archdiocese of Vienna</a>, in which is also vested the exempt <a href="/wiki/Ordinariate" title="Ordinariate">Ordinariate</a> for Byzantine-rite Catholics in Austria; its current <a href="/wiki/Archbishop" title="Archbishop">Archbishop</a> is <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cardinal_(Catholicism)" title="Cardinal (Catholicism)">Cardinal</a> <a href="/wiki/Christoph_Sch%C3%B6nborn" title="Christoph Schönborn">Christoph Schönborn</a>. Many Roman <a href="/wiki/Catholic_Church" title="Catholic Church">Catholic churches</a> in central Vienna feature performances of religious or other music, including masses sung to classical music and organ. Some of Vienna's most significant historical buildings are Roman Catholic churches, including the <a href="/wiki/St._Stephen%27s_Cathedral,_Vienna" title="St. Stephen's Cathedral, Vienna">St. Stephen's Cathedral</a> (<i>Stephansdom</i>), <a href="/wiki/Karlskirche" title="Karlskirche">Karlskirche</a>, <a href="/wiki/Peterskirche,_Vienna" title="Peterskirche, Vienna">Peterskirche</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Votive_Church,_Vienna" title="Votive Church, Vienna">Votivkirche</a>.</p>
<p>The proportion of Viennese who identify as Roman Catholic has dropped over the last fifty years, from 90% in 1961 to 39.8% in 2010.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-105"><a href="#cite_note-105">[105]</a></sup></p>
<p>On the banks of the Danube, there is a Buddhist <a href="/wiki/Peace_Pagoda" title="Peace Pagoda">Peace Pagoda</a>, built in 1983 by the monks and nuns of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nipponzan_Myohoji" title="Nipponzan Myohoji">Nipponzan Myohoji</a>.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Culture">Culture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Vienna&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Culture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Music.2C_theatre_and_opera">Music, theatre and opera</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Vienna&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Music, theatre and opera">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Music_of_Austria" title="Music of Austria">Music of Austria</a> and <a href="/wiki/Vienna_State_Ballet" title="Vienna State Ballet">Vienna State Ballet</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Vienna_-_Johann_Strauss_Monument_in_Stadt_Park_-_4572.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2784" data-file-width="4124" height="149" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/eb/Vienna_-_Johann_Strauss_Monument_in_Stadt_Park_-_4572.jpg/220px-Vienna_-_Johann_Strauss_Monument_in_Stadt_Park_-_4572.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/eb/Vienna_-_Johann_Strauss_Monument_in_Stadt_Park_-_4572.jpg/330px-Vienna_-_Johann_Strauss_Monument_in_Stadt_Park_-_4572.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/eb/Vienna_-_Johann_Strauss_Monument_in_Stadt_Park_-_4572.jpg/440px-Vienna_-_Johann_Strauss_Monument_in_Stadt_Park_-_4572.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Vienna_-_Johann_Strauss_Monument_in_Stadt_Park_-_4572.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Monument of <a href="/wiki/Johann_Strauss_II" title="Johann Strauss II">Johann Strauss II</a> at <a href="/wiki/Stadtpark,_Vienna" title="Stadtpark, Vienna">Stadtpark, Vienna</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Musical luminaries including <a href="/wiki/Wolfgang_Amadeus_Mozart" title="Wolfgang Amadeus Mozart">Wolfgang Amadeus Mozart</a>, <a href="/wiki/Joseph_Haydn" title="Joseph Haydn">Joseph Haydn</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ludwig_van_Beethoven" title="Ludwig van Beethoven">Ludwig van Beethoven</a>, <a href="/wiki/Franz_Schubert" title="Franz Schubert">Franz Schubert</a>, <a href="/wiki/Johannes_Brahms" title="Johannes Brahms">Johannes Brahms</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gustav_Mahler" title="Gustav Mahler">Gustav Mahler</a>, <a href="/wiki/Robert_Stolz" title="Robert Stolz">Robert Stolz</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Arnold_Schoenberg" title="Arnold Schoenberg">Arnold Schoenberg</a> have worked there.</p>
<p>Art and culture had a long tradition in Vienna, including theatre, opera, classical music and fine arts. The <a href="/wiki/Burgtheater" title="Burgtheater">Burgtheater</a> is considered one of the best theatres in the German-speaking world alongside its branch, the Akademietheater. The <a href="/wiki/Volkstheater,_Vienna" title="Volkstheater, Vienna">Volkstheater Wien</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Theater_in_der_Josefstadt" title="Theater in der Josefstadt">Theater in der Josefstadt</a> also enjoy good reputations. There is also a multitude of smaller theatres, in many cases devoted to less mainstream forms of the performing arts, such as modern, experimental plays or <a href="/wiki/Cabaret" title="Cabaret">cabaret</a>.</p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Wiener_Staatsoper_abend.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="591" data-file-width="900" height="144" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3a/Wiener_Staatsoper_abend.jpg/220px-Wiener_Staatsoper_abend.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3a/Wiener_Staatsoper_abend.jpg/330px-Wiener_Staatsoper_abend.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3a/Wiener_Staatsoper_abend.jpg/440px-Wiener_Staatsoper_abend.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Wiener_Staatsoper_abend.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
State Opera (<i>Staatsoper</i>)</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Vienna is also home to a number of opera houses, including the <a href="/wiki/Theater_an_der_Wien" title="Theater an der Wien">Theater an der Wien</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Vienna_State_Opera" title="Vienna State Opera">Staatsoper</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Vienna_Volksoper" title="Vienna Volksoper">Volksoper</a>, the latter being devoted to the typical Viennese <a href="/wiki/Operetta" title="Operetta">operetta</a>. Classical concerts are performed at world-famous venues such as the <a href="/wiki/Musikverein" title="Musikverein">Wiener Musikverein</a>, home of the <a href="/wiki/Vienna_Philharmonic" title="Vienna Philharmonic">Vienna Philharmonic</a> Orchestra known across the world for the annual widely broadcast "New Year's Day Concert", as well as the <a href="/wiki/Konzerthaus,_Vienna" title="Konzerthaus, Vienna">Wiener Konzerthaus</a>, home of the internationally renowned <a href="/wiki/Vienna_Symphony" title="Vienna Symphony">Vienna Symphony</a>. Many concert venues offer concerts aimed at tourists, featuring popular highlights of Viennese music, particularly the works of <a href="/wiki/Wolfgang_Amadeus_Mozart" title="Wolfgang Amadeus Mozart">Wolfgang Amadeus Mozart</a>, Johann Strauss the father, and Johann Strauss the son.</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Wien_-_Neue_Hofburg.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2130" data-file-width="4724" height="99" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/31/Wien_-_Neue_Hofburg.JPG/220px-Wien_-_Neue_Hofburg.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/31/Wien_-_Neue_Hofburg.JPG/330px-Wien_-_Neue_Hofburg.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/31/Wien_-_Neue_Hofburg.JPG/440px-Wien_-_Neue_Hofburg.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Wien_-_Neue_Hofburg.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hofburg_Palace" title="Hofburg Palace">Hofburg Palace</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Musikverein_Wien1.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2448" data-file-width="3264" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dc/Musikverein_Wien1.JPG/220px-Musikverein_Wien1.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dc/Musikverein_Wien1.JPG/330px-Musikverein_Wien1.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dc/Musikverein_Wien1.JPG/440px-Musikverein_Wien1.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Musikverein_Wien1.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Musikverein Vienna</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Up until 2005, the Theater an der Wien has hosted premieres of musicals, although with the year of the Mozart celebrations 2006 it has devoted itself to the opera again and has since become a stagione opera house offering one new production each month, thus quickly becoming one of Europe's most interesting and advanced opera houses. Since 2012 Theater an der Wien has taken over the Wiener Kammeroper, a historical small theatre in the first district of Vienna seating 300 spectators, turning it into its second venue for smaller sized productions and chamber operas created by the young ensemble of Theater an der Wien (JET). Before 2005 the most successful musical was <i><a href="/wiki/Elisabeth_(musical)" title="Elisabeth (musical)">Elisabeth</a></i>, which was later translated into several languages and performed all over the world. The <a href="/wiki/Wiener_Taschenoper" title="Wiener Taschenoper">Wiener Taschenoper</a> is dedicated to stage music of the 20th and 21st century. The <a href="/wiki/Haus_der_Musik" title="Haus der Musik">Haus der Musik</a> ("house of music") opened in the year 2000.</p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Wienerlied" title="Wienerlied">Wienerlied</a> is a unique song genre from Vienna. There are approximately 60,000 – 70,000 Wienerlieder.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-VLW_106-0"><a href="#cite_note-VLW-106">[106]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 1981 the popular British new romantic group <a href="/wiki/Ultravox" title="Ultravox">Ultravox</a> paid a tribute to Vienna on an album and an artful music video recording called <i>Vienna</i>. The inspiration for this work arose from the cinema production called <i><a href="/wiki/The_Third_Man" title="The Third Man">The Third Man</a></i> with the title <a href="/wiki/Zither" title="Zither">Zither</a> music of <a href="/wiki/Anton_Karas" title="Anton Karas">Anton Karas</a>.</p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Vienna%27s_English_Theatre" title="Vienna's English Theatre">Vienna's English Theatre</a> (VET) is an English theater in Vienna. It was founded in 1963 and is located in the 8th Vienna's district. It is the oldest English-language theater in Europe outside the UK.</p>
<p>In May 2015, Vienna hosted the <a href="/wiki/Eurovision_Song_Contest_2015" title="Eurovision Song Contest 2015">60th Annual Eurovision Song Contest</a> following Austria's victory in the <a href="/wiki/Eurovision_Song_Contest_2014" title="Eurovision Song Contest 2014">2014 contest</a>.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Musicians_from_Vienna">Musicians from Vienna</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Vienna&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Musicians from Vienna">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Notable musicians were born in Vienna, including: <a href="/wiki/Franz_Schubert" title="Franz Schubert">Franz Schubert</a>, <a href="/wiki/Joseph_Lanner" title="Joseph Lanner">Joseph Lanner</a>, <a href="/wiki/Johann_Strauss_I" title="Johann Strauss I">Johann Strauss I</a>, <a href="/wiki/Johann_Strauss_II" title="Johann Strauss II">Johann Strauss II</a>, <a href="/wiki/Arnold_Schoenberg" title="Arnold Schoenberg">Arnold Schönberg</a>, <a href="/wiki/Fritz_Kreisler" title="Fritz Kreisler">Fritz Kreisler</a>, <a href="/wiki/Alban_Berg" title="Alban Berg">Alban Berg</a>, <a href="/wiki/Anton_Webern" title="Anton Webern">Anton Webern</a>, <a href="/wiki/Louie_Austen" title="Louie Austen">Louie Austen</a>, <a href="/wiki/Falco_(musician)" title="Falco (musician)">Falco</a> and <a href="/wiki/Joe_Zawinul" title="Joe Zawinul">Joe Zawinul</a>.</p>
<p>Famous musicians who came here to work from other parts of Austria and Germany were <a href="/wiki/Johann_Joseph_Fux" title="Johann Joseph Fux">Johann Joseph Fux</a>, <a href="/wiki/Joseph_Haydn" title="Joseph Haydn">Joseph Haydn</a>, <a href="/wiki/Wolfgang_Amadeus_Mozart" title="Wolfgang Amadeus Mozart">Wolfgang Amadeus Mozart</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ludwig_van_Beethoven" title="Ludwig van Beethoven">Ludwig van Beethoven</a>, <a href="/wiki/Johann_Sedlatzek" title="Johann Sedlatzek">Johann Sedlatzek</a>, <a href="/wiki/Antonio_Salieri" title="Antonio Salieri">Antonio Salieri</a>, <a href="/wiki/Carl_Czerny" title="Carl Czerny">Carl Czerny</a>, <a href="/wiki/Johann_Nepomuk_Hummel" title="Johann Nepomuk Hummel">Johann Nepomuk Hummel</a>, <a href="/wiki/Franz_Liszt" title="Franz Liszt">Franz Liszt</a>, <a href="/wiki/Franz_von_Supp%C3%A9" title="Franz von Suppé">Franz von Suppé</a>, <a href="/wiki/Anton_Bruckner" title="Anton Bruckner">Anton Bruckner</a>, <a href="/wiki/Johannes_Brahms" title="Johannes Brahms">Johannes Brahms</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gustav_Mahler" title="Gustav Mahler">Gustav Mahler</a> and <a href="/wiki/Rainhard_Fendrich" title="Rainhard Fendrich">Rainhard Fendrich</a>.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Famous_Jewish_cultural_figures_from_Vienna">Famous Jewish cultural figures from Vienna</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Vienna&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Famous Jewish cultural figures from Vienna">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Among the most notable Viennese Jews, some of whom left Austria before and during Nazi persecution, are the following international figures: <a href="/wiki/Sigmund_Freud" title="Sigmund Freud">Sigmund Freud</a>, <a href="/wiki/Fritz_Lang" title="Fritz Lang">Fritz Lang</a>, <a href="/wiki/Fred_Zinnemann" title="Fred Zinnemann">Fred Zinnemann</a> (both of whose parents died in the Holocaust), <a href="/wiki/Stefan_Zweig" title="Stefan Zweig">Stefan Zweig</a>, <a href="/wiki/Erich_von_Stroheim" title="Erich von Stroheim">Erich von Stroheim</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hedy_Lamarr" title="Hedy Lamarr">Hedy Lamarr</a>, <a href="/wiki/Franz_Werfel" title="Franz Werfel">Franz Werfel</a>, <a href="/wiki/Arnold_Schoenberg" title="Arnold Schoenberg">Arnold Schoenberg</a> and <a href="/wiki/Fritz_Kreisler" title="Fritz Kreisler">Fritz Kreisler</a>.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Museums">Museums</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Vienna&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Museums">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_museums_in_Vienna" title="List of museums in Vienna">List of museums in Vienna</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Museumsquartier_courtyard.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1900" data-file-width="2795" height="150" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/Museumsquartier_courtyard.jpg/220px-Museumsquartier_courtyard.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/Museumsquartier_courtyard.jpg/330px-Museumsquartier_courtyard.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/Museumsquartier_courtyard.jpg/440px-Museumsquartier_courtyard.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Museumsquartier_courtyard.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Courtyard of the <a href="/wiki/Museumsquartier" title="Museumsquartier">Museumsquartier</a> with <i>Enzi</i> seating furniture</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hofburg_Palace" title="Hofburg Palace">Hofburg</a> is the location of the <a href="/wiki/Imperial_Treasury,_Vienna" title="Imperial Treasury, Vienna">Imperial Treasury</a> (<i>Schatzkammer</i>), holding the imperial jewels of the Habsburg dynasty. The Sisi Museum (a museum devoted to <a href="/wiki/Empress_Elisabeth_of_Austria" title="Empress Elisabeth of Austria">Empress Elisabeth of Austria</a>) allows visitors to view the imperial apartments as well as the silver cabinet. Directly opposite the Hofburg are the <a href="/wiki/Kunsthistorisches_Museum" title="Kunsthistorisches Museum">Kunsthistorisches Museum</a>, which houses many paintings by <a href="/wiki/Old_Master" title="Old Master">old masters</a>, ancient and classical artifacts, and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Naturhistorisches_Museum" title="Naturhistorisches Museum">Naturhistorisches Museum</a>.</p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Vienna_-_Liechtenstein_Museum_and_Library_-_6471.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2912" data-file-width="4368" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/75/Vienna_-_Liechtenstein_Museum_and_Library_-_6471.jpg/220px-Vienna_-_Liechtenstein_Museum_and_Library_-_6471.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/75/Vienna_-_Liechtenstein_Museum_and_Library_-_6471.jpg/330px-Vienna_-_Liechtenstein_Museum_and_Library_-_6471.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/75/Vienna_-_Liechtenstein_Museum_and_Library_-_6471.jpg/440px-Vienna_-_Liechtenstein_Museum_and_Library_-_6471.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Vienna_-_Liechtenstein_Museum_and_Library_-_6471.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Liechtenstein Museum</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>A number of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Museums" title="Museums">museums</a> are located in the <a href="/wiki/Museumsquartier" title="Museumsquartier">Museumsquartier</a> (museum quarter), the former Imperial Stalls which were converted into a museum complex in the 1990s. It houses the Museum of Modern Art, commonly known as the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/MUMOK" title="MUMOK">MUMOK</a> (Ludwig Foundation), the <a href="/wiki/Leopold_Museum" title="Leopold Museum">Leopold Museum</a> (featuring the largest collection of paintings in the world by <a href="/wiki/Egon_Schiele" title="Egon Schiele">Egon Schiele</a>, as well as works by the <a href="/wiki/Vienna_Secession" title="Vienna Secession">Vienna Secession</a>, Viennese Modernism and Austrian Expressionism), the <a href="/wiki/Architekturzentrum_Wien" title="Architekturzentrum Wien">AzW</a> (museum of architecture), additional halls with feature exhibitions, and the Tanzquartier. The Liechtenstein Palace contains much of one of the world's <a href="/wiki/Liechtenstein_Museum" title="Liechtenstein Museum">largest private art collections</a>, especially strong in the <a href="/wiki/Baroque" title="Baroque">Baroque</a>. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Belvedere_(palace)" title="Belvedere (palace)">Castle Belvedere</a>, built under <a href="/wiki/German_cruiser_Prinz_Eugen" title="German cruiser Prinz Eugen">Prinz Eugen</a>, has <a href="/wiki/%C3%96sterreichische_Galerie_Belvedere" title="Österreichische Galerie Belvedere">a gallery</a> containing paintings by <a href="/wiki/Gustav_Klimt" title="Gustav Klimt">Gustav Klimt</a> (The Kiss), Egon Schiele, and other painters of the early 20th century, also sculptures by <a href="/wiki/Franz_Xaver_Messerschmidt" title="Franz Xaver Messerschmidt">Franz Xaver Messerschmidt</a>, and changing exhibitions too.</p>
<p>There are a multitude of other museums in Vienna, including the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Albertina,_Vienna" title="Albertina, Vienna">Albertina</a>, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Heeresgeschichtliches_Museum" title="Heeresgeschichtliches Museum">Military History Museum</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Technisches_Museum_Wien" title="Technisches Museum Wien">Technical Museum</a>, the Burial Museum, the <a href="/wiki/Museum_of_Art_Fakes" title="Museum of Art Fakes">Museum of Art Fakes</a>, the <a href="/wiki/KunstHausWien" title="KunstHausWien">KunstHausWien</a>, <a href="/wiki/Museum_of_Applied_Arts,_Vienna" title="Museum of Applied Arts, Vienna">Museum of Applied Arts</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Sigmund_Freud_Museum_(Vienna)" title="Sigmund Freud Museum (Vienna)">Sigmund Freud Museum</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Mozarthaus_Vienna" title="Mozarthaus Vienna">Mozarthaus Vienna</a>. The museums on the history of the city, including the former <a href="/wiki/Vienna_Museum#Vienna_Museum_Karlsplatz" title="Vienna Museum">Historical Museum of the City of Vienna</a> on <a href="/wiki/Karlsplatz" title="Karlsplatz">Karlsplatz</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Hermesvilla" title="Hermesvilla">Hermesvilla</a>, the residences and birthplaces of various composers, the <a href="/wiki/Vienna_Museum#Museum_of_the_Romans" title="Vienna Museum">Museum of the Romans</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Vienna_Museum#Clock_Museum" title="Vienna Museum">Vienna Clock Museum</a>, are now gathered together under the group umbrella <a href="/wiki/Vienna_Museum" title="Vienna Museum">Vienna Museum</a>. In addition there are museums dedicated to Vienna's individual districts. They provide a record of individual struggles, achievements and tragedy as the city grew and survived two world wars. For readers seeking family histories these are good sources of information.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Architecture">Architecture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Vienna&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Architecture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Category:Buildings_and_structures_in_Austria" title="Category:Buildings and structures in Austria">Category:Buildings and structures in Austria</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Palais_Ferstl_Vienna_June_2006_002.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2560" data-file-width="1920" height="227" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bc/Palais_Ferstl_Vienna_June_2006_002.jpg/170px-Palais_Ferstl_Vienna_June_2006_002.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bc/Palais_Ferstl_Vienna_June_2006_002.jpg/255px-Palais_Ferstl_Vienna_June_2006_002.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bc/Palais_Ferstl_Vienna_June_2006_002.jpg/340px-Palais_Ferstl_Vienna_June_2006_002.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Palais_Ferstl_Vienna_June_2006_002.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Palais Ferstel</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Wien_Hotel_Sacher_Am_Abend.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1790" data-file-width="2135" height="184" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/36/Wien_Hotel_Sacher_Am_Abend.jpg/220px-Wien_Hotel_Sacher_Am_Abend.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/36/Wien_Hotel_Sacher_Am_Abend.jpg/330px-Wien_Hotel_Sacher_Am_Abend.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/36/Wien_Hotel_Sacher_Am_Abend.jpg/440px-Wien_Hotel_Sacher_Am_Abend.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Wien_Hotel_Sacher_Am_Abend.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Hotel_Sacher" title="Hotel Sacher">Hotel Sacher</a> at night</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>A variety of architectural styles can be found in Vienna, such as the <a href="/wiki/Romanesque_architecture" title="Romanesque architecture">Romanesque</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ruprechtskirche" title="Ruprechtskirche">Ruprechtskirche</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Baroque_architecture" title="Baroque architecture">Baroque</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/St._Charles%27s_Church,_Vienna" title="St. Charles's Church, Vienna">Karlskirche</a>. Styles range from <a href="/wiki/Classicism" title="Classicism">classicist</a> buildings to <a href="/wiki/Modern_architecture" title="Modern architecture">modern architecture</a>. <a href="/wiki/Art_Nouveau" title="Art Nouveau">Art Nouveau</a> left many architectural traces in Vienna. The <a href="/wiki/Vienna_Secession" title="Vienna Secession">Secession</a>, <a href="/wiki/Karlsplatz_Stadtbahn_Station" title="Karlsplatz Stadtbahn Station">Karlsplatz Stadtbahn Station</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Kirche_am_Steinhof" title="Kirche am Steinhof">Kirche am Steinhof</a> by <a href="/wiki/Otto_Wagner" title="Otto Wagner">Otto Wagner</a> rank among the best known examples of Art Nouveau in the world. Wagner's prominent student <a href="/wiki/Jo%C5%BEe_Ple%C4%8Dnik" title="Jože Plečnik">Jože Plečnik</a> from <a href="/wiki/Slovenia" title="Slovenia">Slovenia</a> also left important traces in Vienna. His works include the Langer House (1900) and the <a href="/wiki/Zacherlhaus" title="Zacherlhaus">Zacherlhaus</a> (1903–1905). Plečnik's 1910–1913 <i>Church of the Holy Spirit</i> (<a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Heilig-Geist-Kirche&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Heilig-Geist-Kirche (page does not exist)">Heilig-Geist-Kirche</a><span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;"> (<a class="extiw" href="https://de.wikipedia.org/wiki/Heilig-Geist-Kirche_(Wien)" title="de:Heilig-Geist-Kirche (Wien)">de</a>)</span>) in Vienna is remarkable for its innovative use of poured-in-place concrete as both structure and exterior surface, and also for its abstracted classical form language. Most radical is the church's crypt, with its slender concrete columns and angular, cubist capitals and bases.</p>
<p>Concurrent to the Art Nouveau movement was the <a href="/wiki/Wiener_Moderne" title="Wiener Moderne">Wiener Moderne</a>, during which some architects shunned the use of extraneous adornment. A key architect of this period was <a href="/wiki/Adolf_Loos" title="Adolf Loos">Adolf Loos</a>, whose works include the Looshaus (1909), the Kärntner Bar or American Bar (1908) and the <a href="/wiki/Steiner_House" title="Steiner House">Steiner House</a> (1910).</p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Hundertwasserhaus" title="Hundertwasserhaus">Hundertwasserhaus</a> by <a href="/wiki/Friedensreich_Hundertwasser" title="Friedensreich Hundertwasser">Friedensreich Hundertwasser</a>, designed to counter the clinical look of modern architecture, is one of Vienna's most popular <a href="/wiki/Tourist_attraction" title="Tourist attraction">tourist attractions</a>. Another example of unique architecture is the <a href="/wiki/Wotruba_Church" title="Wotruba Church">Wotrubakirche</a> by sculptor <a href="/wiki/Fritz_Wotruba" title="Fritz Wotruba">Fritz Wotruba</a>. In the 1990s, a number of quarters were adapted and extensive building projects were implemented in the areas around Donaustadt (north of the Danube) and Wienerberg (in southern Vienna).</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Stephansdom_Vienna_July_2008_(27)-Stephansdom_Vienna_July_2008_(31).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3192" data-file-width="4440" height="158" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c8/Stephansdom_Vienna_July_2008_%2827%29-Stephansdom_Vienna_July_2008_%2831%29.jpg/220px-Stephansdom_Vienna_July_2008_%2827%29-Stephansdom_Vienna_July_2008_%2831%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c8/Stephansdom_Vienna_July_2008_%2827%29-Stephansdom_Vienna_July_2008_%2831%29.jpg/330px-Stephansdom_Vienna_July_2008_%2827%29-Stephansdom_Vienna_July_2008_%2831%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c8/Stephansdom_Vienna_July_2008_%2827%29-Stephansdom_Vienna_July_2008_%2831%29.jpg/440px-Stephansdom_Vienna_July_2008_%2827%29-Stephansdom_Vienna_July_2008_%2831%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Stephansdom_Vienna_July_2008_(27)-Stephansdom_Vienna_July_2008_(31).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Panoramic view of the city from Stephansdom</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The 220-meter high <a href="/wiki/DC_Towers" title="DC Towers">DC Tower 1</a> located on the Northern bank of the Danube, completed in 2013, is the talltest skyscraper in Vienna.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-107"><a href="#cite_note-107">[107]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-108"><a href="#cite_note-108">[108]</a></sup> In recent years, Vienna has seen numerous architecture projects completed which combine modern architectural elements with old buildings, such as the remodelling and revitalisation of the old <a href="/wiki/Gasometer,_Vienna" title="Gasometer, Vienna">Gasometer</a> in 2001. Most buildings in Vienna are relatively low; in early 2006 there were around 100 buildings higher than 40 metres (130 feet). The number of high-rise buildings is kept low by building legislation aimed at preserving green areas and districts designated as <a href="/wiki/World_Heritage_Site" title="World Heritage Site">world cultural heritage</a>. Strong rules apply to the planning, authorisation and construction of high-rise buildings. Consequently, much of the inner city is a high-rise free zone.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Vienna_balls">Vienna balls</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Vienna&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Vienna balls">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Vienna is the last great capital of the 19th-century <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ball_(dance)" title="Ball (dance)">ball</a>. There are over 450 balls per year, some featuring as many as nine live orchestras.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Vienna_Tourist_Board_109-0"><a href="#cite_note-Vienna_Tourist_Board-109">[109]</a></sup> Balls are held in the many beautiful palaces in Vienna, with the principal venue being the Hofburg Palace in <a href="/wiki/Heldenplatz" title="Heldenplatz">Heldenplatz</a>. While the <a href="/wiki/Vienna_Opera_Ball" title="Vienna Opera Ball">Opera Ball</a> is the best known internationally of all the Austrian balls, <a href="/wiki/List_of_balls_in_Vienna" title="List of balls in Vienna">other balls</a> such as the Kaffeesiederball (Cafe Owners Ball), the Jägerball (Hunter's Ball) and the <a href="/wiki/Life_Ball" title="Life Ball">Life Ball</a> (AIDS charity event) are almost as well known within Austria and even better appreciated for their cordial atmosphere. Viennese of at least middle class may visit a number of balls in their lifetime.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="margin-left:0.1em; white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Please_clarify" title="Wikipedia:Please clarify"><span title="The text near this tag may need clarification or removal of jargon. (May 2016)">clarification needed</span></a></i>]</sup> For many, the ball season lasts three months and can include up to ten or fifteen separate appearances.</p>
<p>Dancers and opera singers from the <a href="/wiki/Vienna_State_Opera" title="Vienna State Opera">Vienna State Opera</a> often perform at the openings of the larger balls.</p>
<p>A Vienna ball is an all-night cultural attraction. Major Viennese balls generally begin at 9 pm and last until 5 am, although many guests carry on the celebrations into the next day.The Viennese balls are being exported with the support of the City of Vienna in around 30 cities worldwide such as New York, Barcelona, Hong Kong, Kuala Lumpur, Rome, Prague, Bucharest, Berlin and Moscow.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Vienna_Tourist_Board_109-1"><a href="#cite_note-Vienna_Tourist_Board-109">[109]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-110"><a href="#cite_note-110">[110]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-111"><a href="#cite_note-111">[111]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Education">Education</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Vienna&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Education">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Vienna is Austria's main centre of education and home to many universities, professional colleges and <a href="/wiki/Gymnasium_(school)" title="Gymnasium (school)">gymnasiums (high schools)</a>.</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Friedrich_von_Schiller.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2848" data-file-width="4272" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cb/Friedrich_von_Schiller.JPG/220px-Friedrich_von_Schiller.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cb/Friedrich_von_Schiller.JPG/330px-Friedrich_von_Schiller.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cb/Friedrich_von_Schiller.JPG/440px-Friedrich_von_Schiller.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a>
