<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Leisure_activities">Leisure activities</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Vienna&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Leisure activities">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Parks_and_gardens">Parks and gardens</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Vienna&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Parks and gardens">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Volksgarten_Vienna_June_2006_300.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1920" data-file-width="2560" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a8/Volksgarten_Vienna_June_2006_300.jpg/220px-Volksgarten_Vienna_June_2006_300.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a8/Volksgarten_Vienna_June_2006_300.jpg/330px-Volksgarten_Vienna_June_2006_300.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a8/Volksgarten_Vienna_June_2006_300.jpg/440px-Volksgarten_Vienna_June_2006_300.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Volksgarten_Vienna_June_2006_300.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Vienna city park</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Vienna possesses many parks, including the <i><a href="/wiki/Stadtpark,_Vienna" title="Stadtpark, Vienna">Stadtpark</a></i>, the <i>Burggarten</i>, the <i>Volksgarten</i> (part of the <i>Hofburg</i>), the <i>Schlosspark</i> at Schloss Belvedere (home to the <a href="/wiki/Botanical_Garden_of_the_University_of_Vienna" title="Botanical Garden of the University of Vienna">Vienna Botanic Gardens</a>), the <i>Donaupark</i>, the <i>Schönbrunner Schlosspark</i>, the <i><a href="/wiki/Prater" title="Prater">Prater</a></i>, the <i>Augarten</i>, the <i>Rathauspark</i>, the <i><a href="/wiki/Lainzer_Tiergarten" title="Lainzer Tiergarten">Lainzer Tiergarten</a></i>, the <i>Dehnepark</i>, the <i>Resselpark</i>, the <i>Votivpark</i>, the <i>Kurpark Oberlaa</i>, the <i>Auer-Welsbach-Park</i> and the <i>Türkenschanzpark</i>. Green areas include <i>Laaer-Berg</i> (including the Bohemian Prater) and the foothills of the <i><a href="/wiki/Vienna_Woods" title="Vienna Woods">Wienerwald</a></i>, which reaches into the outer areas of the city. Small parks, known by the Viennese as <i>Beserlparks</i>, are everywhere in the inner city areas.</p>
<p>Many of Vienna's famous parks include monuments, such as the <a href="/wiki/Stadtpark,_Vienna" title="Stadtpark, Vienna">Stadtpark</a> with its statue of <a href="/wiki/Johann_Strauss_II" title="Johann Strauss II">Johann Strauss II</a>, and the gardens of the <a href="/wiki/Baroque" title="Baroque">baroque</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Belvedere_(palace)" title="Belvedere (palace)">palace</a>, where the <a href="/wiki/Austrian_State_Treaty" title="Austrian State Treaty">State Treaty</a> was signed. Vienna's principal park is the <a href="/wiki/Prater" title="Prater">Prater</a> which is home to the <a href="/wiki/Wiener_Riesenrad" title="Wiener Riesenrad">Riesenrad</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Ferris_wheel" title="Ferris wheel">Ferris wheel</a>. The imperial <a href="/wiki/Sch%C3%B6nbrunn_Palace" title="Schönbrunn Palace">Schönbrunn</a>'s grounds contain an 18th-century park which includes <a href="/wiki/Tiergarten_Sch%C3%B6nbrunn" title="Tiergarten Schönbrunn">the world's oldest zoo</a>, founded in 1752. The <a href="/wiki/Donauinsel" title="Donauinsel">Donauinsel</a>, part of Vienna's flood defences, is a 21.1 km (13.1 mi) long <a href="/wiki/Artificial_island" title="Artificial island">artificial island</a> between the Danube and Neue Donau dedicated to leisure activities.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sport">Sport</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Vienna&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: Sport">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Ernst_Happel_Stadion.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1944" data-file-width="2592" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d6/Ernst_Happel_Stadion.jpg/220px-Ernst_Happel_Stadion.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d6/Ernst_Happel_Stadion.jpg/330px-Ernst_Happel_Stadion.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d6/Ernst_Happel_Stadion.jpg/440px-Ernst_Happel_Stadion.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Ernst_Happel_Stadion.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Ernst-Happel-Stadion" title="Ernst-Happel-Stadion">Ernst-Happel-Stadion</a> in the Prater</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Austria's capital is home to numerous <a href="/wiki/Association_football" title="Association football">football</a> teams. The best known are the local football clubs include <a href="/wiki/FK_Austria_Wien" title="FK Austria Wien">FK Austria Wien</a> (21 <a href="/wiki/Austrian_Football_Bundesliga" title="Austrian Football Bundesliga">Austrian Bundesliga</a> titles and record 27-time cup winners), <a href="/wiki/SK_Rapid_Wien" title="SK Rapid Wien">SK Rapid Wien</a> (record 32 <a href="/wiki/Austrian_Football_Bundesliga" title="Austrian Football Bundesliga">Austrian Bundesliga</a> titles), and the oldest team, <a href="/wiki/First_Vienna_FC" title="First Vienna FC">First Vienna FC</a>. Other important <a href="/wiki/Sports_club" title="Sports club">sports clubs</a> include the <a href="/wiki/Vikings_Vienna" title="Vikings Vienna">Raiffeisen Vikings Vienna</a> (<a href="/wiki/American_football" title="American football">American Football</a>), who won the <a href="/wiki/Eurobowl" title="Eurobowl">Eurobowl</a> title between 2004 and 2007 4 times in a row and had a perfect season in 2013, the <a href="/wiki/Aon_hotVolleys_Vienna" title="Aon hotVolleys Vienna">Aon hotVolleys Vienna</a>, one of Europe's premier Volleyball organisations, the Vienna Wanderers (baseball) who won the 2012 and 2013 Championship of the Austrian Baseball League, and the <a href="/wiki/Vienna_Capitals" title="Vienna Capitals">Vienna Capitals</a> (<a href="/wiki/Ice_hockey" title="Ice hockey">Ice Hockey</a>). Vienna was also where the European Handball Federation (EHF) was founded. There are also three <a href="/wiki/Rugby_union" title="Rugby union">rugby</a> clubs; <a href="/wiki/Vienna_Celtic_RFC" title="Vienna Celtic RFC">Vienna Celtic</a>, the oldest rugby club in Austria, <a href="/wiki/RC_Donau" title="RC Donau">RC Donau</a>, and Stade Viennois</p>
<p>Vienna hosts many different sporting events including the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Vienna_Marathon" title="Vienna Marathon">Vienna City Marathon</a>, which attracts more than 10,000 participants every year and normally takes place in May. In 2005 the <a href="/wiki/Ice_hockey" title="Ice hockey">Ice Hockey</a> World Championships took place in <a href="/wiki/Austria" title="Austria">Austria</a> and the final was played in Vienna. Vienna's <a href="/wiki/Ernst-Happel-Stadion" title="Ernst-Happel-Stadion">Ernst Happel Stadium</a> was the venue of four <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Champions_League" title="UEFA Champions League">Champions League</a> and European Champion Clubs' Cup finals (1964, 1987, 1990 and 1995) and on 29 June it hosted the final of <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Euro_2008" title="UEFA Euro 2008">Euro 2008</a> which saw a Spanish 1–0 victory over Germany. <a href="/wiki/Tennis" title="Tennis">Tennis</a> tournament <a href="/wiki/Vienna_Open" title="Vienna Open">Vienna Open</a> also takes place in the city since 1974. The matches are played in the <a href="/wiki/Wiener_Stadthalle" title="Wiener Stadthalle">Wiener Stadthalle</a>.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Culinary_specialities">Culinary specialities</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Vienna&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: Culinary specialities">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Food">Food</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Vienna&amp;action=edit&amp;section=36" title="Edit section: Food">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Austrian_cuisine" title="Austrian cuisine">Austrian cuisine</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Wiener-Schnitzel02.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="952" data-file-width="1298" height="161" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ae/Wiener-Schnitzel02.jpg/220px-Wiener-Schnitzel02.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ae/Wiener-Schnitzel02.jpg/330px-Wiener-Schnitzel02.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ae/Wiener-Schnitzel02.jpg/440px-Wiener-Schnitzel02.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Wiener-Schnitzel02.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<i><a href="/wiki/Wiener_Schnitzel" title="Wiener Schnitzel">Wiener Schnitzel</a></i></div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Sachertorte_DSC03027.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1944" data-file-width="2592" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/Sachertorte_DSC03027.JPG/220px-Sachertorte_DSC03027.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/Sachertorte_DSC03027.JPG/330px-Sachertorte_DSC03027.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/Sachertorte_DSC03027.JPG/440px-Sachertorte_DSC03027.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Sachertorte_DSC03027.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<i><a href="/wiki/Sachertorte" title="Sachertorte">Sachertorte</a></i></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Vienna is well known for <i><a href="/wiki/Wiener_Schnitzel" title="Wiener Schnitzel">Wiener Schnitzel</a></i>, a cutlet of <a href="/wiki/Veal" title="Veal">veal</a> <i>(Kalbsschnitzel)</i> or pork <i>(Schweinsschnitzel)</i> that is pounded flat, coated in flour, egg and breadcrumbs, and fried in <a href="/wiki/Clarified_butter" title="Clarified butter">clarified butter</a>. It is available in almost every restaurant that serves <a href="/wiki/Viennese_cuisine" title="Viennese cuisine">Viennese cuisine</a> and can be eaten hot or cold. The traditional 'Wiener Schnitzel' though is a cutlet of veal. Other examples of Viennese cuisine include <i><a href="/wiki/Tafelspitz" title="Tafelspitz">Tafelspitz</a></i> (very lean boiled beef), which is traditionally served with <i>Geröstete Erdäpfel</i> (boiled potatoes mashed with a fork and subsequently fried) and horseradish sauce, <i>Apfelkren</i> (a mixture of horseradish, cream and apple) and <i>Schnittlauchsauce</i> (a chives sauce made with mayonnaise and stale bread).</p>
<p>Vienna has a long tradition of producing cakes and desserts. These include <i><a href="/wiki/Apple_strudel" title="Apple strudel">Apfelstrudel</a></i> (hot apple strudel), <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Milchrahmstrudel" title="Milchrahmstrudel">Milchrahmstrudel</a></i> (milk-cream strudel), <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Palatschinken" title="Palatschinken">Palatschinken</a></i> (sweet pancakes), and <i>Knödel</i> (dumplings) often filled with fruit such as apricots (<i><a href="/wiki/Marillenkn%C3%B6del" title="Marillenknödel">Marillenknödel</a></i>). <a href="/wiki/Sachertorte" title="Sachertorte">Sachertorte</a>, a delicately moist chocolate cake with apricot jam created by the <a href="/wiki/Hotel_Sacher" title="Hotel Sacher">Sacher Hotel</a>, is world-famous.</p>
<p>In winter, small street stands sell traditional <i>Maroni</i> (hot chestnuts) and potato fritters.</p>
<p>Sausages are popular and available from street vendors (<i><a href="/wiki/W%C3%BCrstelstand" title="Würstelstand">Würstelstand</a></i>) throughout the day and into the night. The sausage known as <i>Wiener</i> (German for Viennese) in the U.S. and in Germany, is called a <i>Frankfurter</i> in Vienna. Other popular sausages are <i>Burenwurst</i> (a coarse beef and pork sausage, generally boiled), <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kranjska_klobasa" title="Kranjska klobasa">Käsekrainer</a></i> (spicy pork with small chunks of cheese), and <i>Bratwurst</i> (a white pork sausage). Most can be ordered "mit Brot" (with bread) or as a "hot dog" (stuffed inside a long roll). Mustard is the traditional condiment and usually offered in two varieties: "süß" (sweet) or "scharf" (spicy).</p>
<p>Kebab, pizza and noodles are, increasingly, the snack foods most widely available from small stands.</p>
<p>The <i><a href="/wiki/Naschmarkt" title="Naschmarkt">Naschmarkt</a></i> is a permanent market for fruit, vegetables, spices, fish, meat, etc., from around the world. The city has many coffee and breakfast stores.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Drinks">Drinks</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Vienna&amp;action=edit&amp;section=37" title="Edit section: Drinks">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Vienna, along with <a href="/wiki/Paris" title="Paris">Paris</a>, <a href="/wiki/Santiago" title="Santiago">Santiago</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cape_Town" title="Cape Town">Cape Town</a>, <a href="/wiki/Prague" title="Prague">Prague</a>, <a href="/wiki/Canberra" title="Canberra">Canberra</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bratislava" title="Bratislava">Bratislava</a>, <a href="/wiki/Warsaw" title="Warsaw">Warsaw</a> and <a href="/wiki/London" title="London">London</a><sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (December 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>, is one of the few remaining world capital cities with its own vineyards. The wine is served in small Viennese pubs known as <a href="/wiki/Heuriger" title="Heuriger">Heuriger</a>, which are especially numerous in the wine growing areas of <a href="/wiki/D%C3%B6bling" title="Döbling">Döbling</a> (<a href="/wiki/Grinzing" title="Grinzing">Grinzing</a>, <a href="/wiki/Neustift_am_Walde" title="Neustift am Walde">Neustift am Walde</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nu%C3%9Fdorf,_Vienna" title="Nußdorf, Vienna">Nußdorf</a>, <a href="/wiki/Salmannsdorf" title="Salmannsdorf">Salmannsdorf</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sievering" title="Sievering">Sievering</a>), <a href="/wiki/Floridsdorf" title="Floridsdorf">Floridsdorf</a> (Stammersdorf, Strebersdorf), <a href="/wiki/Liesing" title="Liesing">Liesing</a> (<a href="/wiki/Mauer,_Vienna" title="Mauer, Vienna">Mauer</a>) and Favoriten (Oberlaa). The wine is often drunk as a Spritzer ("G'spritzter") with sparkling water. The <a href="/wiki/Gr%C3%BCner_Veltliner" title="Grüner Veltliner">Grüner Veltliner</a>, a dry white wine, is the most widely cultivated wine in Austria.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-112"><a href="#cite_note-112">[112]</a></sup></p>
<p>Beer is next in importance to wine. Vienna has a single large brewery, <a href="/wiki/Brauerei_Ottakringer" title="Brauerei Ottakringer">Ottakringer</a>, and more than ten <a href="/wiki/Vienna_microbreweries" title="Vienna microbreweries">microbreweries</a>. A "Beisl" is a typical small Austrian pub, of which Vienna has many.</p>
<p>Also, local soft drinks such as <a href="/wiki/Almdudler" title="Almdudler">Almdudler</a> are very popular around the country as an alternative to alcoholic beverages, placing it on the top spots along American counterparts such as <a href="/wiki/Coca-Cola" title="Coca-Cola">Coca-Cola</a> in terms of market share. Another popular drink is the so-called "<a href="/wiki/Spezi" title="Spezi">Spezi</a>", a mix between <a href="/wiki/Coca-Cola" title="Coca-Cola">Coca-Cola</a> and the original formula of <a href="/wiki/Fanta" title="Fanta">Orange Fanta</a> or the more locally renowned <a href="/wiki/Frucade" title="Frucade">Frucade</a>.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Viennese_caf.C3.A9s">Viennese cafés</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Vienna&amp;action=edit&amp;section=38" title="Edit section: Viennese cafés">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Caf%C3%A9_Demel_interior4,_Vienna.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2560" data-file-width="1920" height="227" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/29/Caf%C3%A9_Demel_interior4%2C_Vienna.jpg/170px-Caf%C3%A9_Demel_interior4%2C_Vienna.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/29/Caf%C3%A9_Demel_interior4%2C_Vienna.jpg/255px-Caf%C3%A9_Demel_interior4%2C_Vienna.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/29/Caf%C3%A9_Demel_interior4%2C_Vienna.jpg/340px-Caf%C3%A9_Demel_interior4%2C_Vienna.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Caf%C3%A9_Demel_interior4,_Vienna.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<i>Demel Café</i></div>
</div>
</div>
<p><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Viennese_caf%C3%A9" title="Viennese café">Viennese cafés</a> have an extremely long and distinguished history that dates back centuries, and the caffeine addictions of some famous historical patrons of the oldest are something of a local legend. These coffee houses are unique to Vienna and many cities have unsuccessfully sought to copy them. Some people consider cafés as their extended living room where nobody will be bothered if they spend hours reading a newspaper while enjoying their coffee. Traditionally, the coffee comes with a glass of water. Viennese cafés claim to have invented the process of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Drip_brew" title="Drip brew">filtering coffee</a> from booty captured after the second <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Vienna" title="Battle of Vienna">Turkish siege</a> in 1683. Viennese cafés claim that when the invading Turks left Vienna, they abandoned hundreds of sacks of <a href="/wiki/Coffee" title="Coffee">coffee</a> beans. The <a href="/wiki/Crown_of_the_Kingdom_of_Poland" title="Crown of the Kingdom of Poland">Polish</a> King <a href="/wiki/John_III_Sobieski" title="John III Sobieski">John III Sobieski</a>, the commander of the anti-Turkish coalition of Poles, Germans, and Austrians, gave <a href="/wiki/Jerzy_Franciszek_Kulczycki" title="Jerzy Franciszek Kulczycki">Franz George Kolschitzky</a> (Polish – <a href="/wiki/Jerzy_Franciszek_Kulczycki" title="Jerzy Franciszek Kulczycki">Franciszek Jerzy Kulczycki</a>) some of this coffee as a reward for providing information that allowed him to defeat the Turks. Kolschitzky then opened Vienna's first <a href="/wiki/Coffeehouse" title="Coffeehouse">coffee shop</a>. <a href="/wiki/Julius_Meinl" title="Julius Meinl">Julius Meinl</a> set up a modern roasting plant in the same premises where the coffee sacks were found, in 1891.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Tourist_attractions">Tourist attractions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Vienna&amp;action=edit&amp;section=39" title="Edit section: Tourist attractions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Tourist_attractions_in_Vienna" title="Tourist attractions in Vienna">Tourist attractions in Vienna</a></div>
<p>Major tourist attractions include the imperial palaces of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hofburg_Imperial_Palace" title="Hofburg Imperial Palace">Hofburg</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sch%C3%B6nbrunn_Palace" title="Schönbrunn Palace">Schönbrunn</a> (also home to the world's oldest zoo, <a href="/wiki/Tiergarten_Sch%C3%B6nbrunn" title="Tiergarten Schönbrunn">Tiergarten Schönbrunn</a>) and the <a href="/wiki/Wiener_Riesenrad" title="Wiener Riesenrad">Riesenrad</a> in the Prater. Cultural highlights include the <a href="/wiki/Burgtheater" title="Burgtheater">Burgtheater</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Vienna_State_Opera" title="Vienna State Opera">Wiener Staatsoper</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Lipizzan" title="Lipizzan">Lipizzaner</a> horses at the <a href="/wiki/Spanish_Riding_School" title="Spanish Riding School">spanische Hofreitschule</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Vienna_Boys%27_Choir" title="Vienna Boys' Choir">Vienna Boys' Choir</a>, as well as excursions to Vienna's Heurigen district Döbling.</p>
<div class="thumb tnone" style="margin-left: auto; margin-right:auto; width:99%; max-width:808px;">
<div class="thumbinner" style="">
<div class="overflowbugx" style="overflow:auto;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Sch%C3%B6nbrunn,_Viede%C5%88,_Rak%C3%BAsko.jpg" title="Schönbrunn Palace"><img alt="" data-file-height="1835" data-file-width="7453" height="197" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7f/Sch%C3%B6nbrunn%2C_Viede%C5%88%2C_Rak%C3%BAsko.jpg/800px-Sch%C3%B6nbrunn%2C_Viede%C5%88%2C_Rak%C3%BAsko.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7f/Sch%C3%B6nbrunn%2C_Viede%C5%88%2C_Rak%C3%BAsko.jpg/1200px-Sch%C3%B6nbrunn%2C_Viede%C5%88%2C_Rak%C3%BAsko.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7f/Sch%C3%B6nbrunn%2C_Viede%C5%88%2C_Rak%C3%BAsko.jpg/1600px-Sch%C3%B6nbrunn%2C_Viede%C5%88%2C_Rak%C3%BAsko.jpg 2x" width="800"/></a></div>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Sch%C3%B6nbrunn,_Viede%C5%88,_Rak%C3%BAsko.jpg" title="File:Schönbrunn, Viedeň, Rakúsko.jpg"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Sch%C3%B6nbrunn_Palace" title="Schönbrunn Palace">Schönbrunn Palace</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tnone" style="margin-left: auto; margin-right:auto; width:99%; max-width:808px;">
<div class="thumbinner" style="">
<div class="overflowbugx" style="overflow:auto;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Schlosspark_Schoenbrunn_Panorama.jpg" title="Gloriette at the Schönbrunn Palace"><img alt="" data-file-height="1610" data-file-width="8521" height="151" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/58/Schlosspark_Schoenbrunn_Panorama.jpg/800px-Schlosspark_Schoenbrunn_Panorama.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/58/Schlosspark_Schoenbrunn_Panorama.jpg/1200px-Schlosspark_Schoenbrunn_Panorama.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/58/Schlosspark_Schoenbrunn_Panorama.jpg/1600px-Schlosspark_Schoenbrunn_Panorama.jpg 2x" width="800"/></a></div>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Schlosspark_Schoenbrunn_Panorama.jpg" title="File:Schlosspark Schoenbrunn Panorama.jpg"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Gloriette" title="Gloriette">Gloriette</a> at the <a href="/wiki/Sch%C3%B6nbrunn_Palace" title="Schönbrunn Palace">Schönbrunn Palace</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>There are also more than 100 art museums, which together attract over eight million visitors per year.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-population_113-0"><a href="#cite_note-population-113">[113]</a></sup> The most popular ones are <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Albertina,_Vienna" title="Albertina, Vienna">Albertina</a>, <a href="/wiki/%C3%96sterreichische_Galerie_Belvedere" title="Österreichische Galerie Belvedere">Belvedere</a>, <a href="/wiki/Leopold_Museum" title="Leopold Museum">Leopold Museum</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Museumsquartier" title="Museumsquartier">Museumsquartier</a>, <a href="/wiki/KunstHausWien" title="KunstHausWien">KunstHausWien</a>, BA-CA Kunstforum, the twin <i><a href="/wiki/Kunsthistorisches_Museum" title="Kunsthistorisches Museum">Kunsthistorisches Museum</a></i> and <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Naturhistorisches_Museum" title="Naturhistorisches Museum">Naturhistorisches Museum</a></i>, and the <a href="/wiki/Technisches_Museum_Wien" title="Technisches Museum Wien">Technisches Museum Wien</a>, each of which receives over a quarter of a million visitors per year.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-114"><a href="#cite_note-114">[114]</a></sup></p>
<p>There are many popular sites associated with composers who lived in Vienna including <a href="/wiki/Ludwig_van_Beethoven" title="Ludwig van Beethoven">Beethoven's</a> various residences and grave at <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Zentralfriedhof" title="Zentralfriedhof">Zentralfriedhof</a> (Central Cemetery) which is the largest cemetery in Vienna and the burial site of many <a href="/wiki/Celebrity" title="Celebrity">famous people</a>. <a href="/wiki/Wolfgang_Amadeus_Mozart" title="Wolfgang Amadeus Mozart">Mozart</a> has a memorial grave at the Habsburg gardens and at <a href="/wiki/St._Marx_Cemetery" title="St. Marx Cemetery">St. Marx cemetery</a> (where his grave was lost). Vienna's many churches also draw large crowds, famous of which are <a href="/wiki/St._Stephen%27s_Cathedral,_Vienna" title="St. Stephen's Cathedral, Vienna">St. Stephen's Cathedral</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Church_of_the_Teutonic_Order,_Vienna" title="Church of the Teutonic Order, Vienna">Deutschordenskirche</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Jesuit_Church,_Vienna" title="Jesuit Church, Vienna">Jesuitenkirche</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Karlskirche" title="Karlskirche">Karlskirche</a>, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Peterskirche" title="Peterskirche">Peterskirche</a>, <a href="/wiki/Maria_am_Gestade" title="Maria am Gestade">Maria am Gestade</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Minoritenkirche" title="Minoritenkirche">Minoritenkirche</a>, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ruprechtskirche" title="Ruprechtskirche">Ruprechtskirche</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Schottenkirche,_Vienna" title="Schottenkirche, Vienna">Schottenkirche</a>, <a href="/wiki/St._Ulrich,_Vienna" title="St. Ulrich, Vienna">St. Ulrich</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Votive_Church,_Vienna" title="Votive Church, Vienna">Votivkirche</a>.</p>
<p>Modern attractions include the <a href="/wiki/Hundertwasserhaus" title="Hundertwasserhaus">Hundertwasserhaus</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Vienna_International_Centre" title="Vienna International Centre">United Nations headquarters</a> and the view from the <a href="/wiki/Donauturm" title="Donauturm">Donauturm</a>.</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Transportation">Transportation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Vienna&amp;action=edit&amp;section=40" title="Edit section: Transportation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:U_Stephansplatz_2.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2736" data-file-width="3648" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6a/U_Stephansplatz_2.JPG/220px-U_Stephansplatz_2.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6a/U_Stephansplatz_2.JPG/330px-U_Stephansplatz_2.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6a/U_Stephansplatz_2.JPG/440px-U_Stephansplatz_2.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:U_Stephansplatz_2.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Stephansplatz_(Vienna_U-Bahn)" title="Stephansplatz (Vienna U-Bahn)">Stephansplatz metro station</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Skylink_landside_3.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="485" data-file-width="1900" height="56" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1d/Skylink_landside_3.jpg/220px-Skylink_landside_3.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1d/Skylink_landside_3.jpg/330px-Skylink_landside_3.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1d/Skylink_landside_3.jpg/440px-Skylink_landside_3.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Skylink_landside_3.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Vienna Airport terminal 3 arrivals lounge</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Transportation_in_Vienna" title="Transportation in Vienna">Transportation in Vienna</a></div>
<p>Vienna has an extensive transportation network with a unified fare system that integrates municipal, regional and railway systems under the umbrella of the Verkehrsverbund Ost-Region (VOR). Public transport is provided by buses, trams and 5 underground metro lines (<a href="/wiki/Vienna_U-Bahn" title="Vienna U-Bahn">U-Bahn</a>). There are also more than 50 <a href="/wiki/Vienna_S-Bahn" title="Vienna S-Bahn">S-train</a> stations within the city limits. Trains are operated by the <a href="/wiki/Austrian_Federal_Railways" title="Austrian Federal Railways">ÖBB</a>. The city forms the hub of the Austrian railway system, with services to all parts of the country and abroad. The railway system connects Vienna with other European cities, like <a href="/wiki/Munich" title="Munich">Munich</a>, <a href="/wiki/Venice" title="Venice">Venice</a>, <a href="/wiki/Budapest" title="Budapest">Budapest</a>, <a href="/wiki/Prague" title="Prague">Prague</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bratislava" title="Bratislava">Bratislava</a> and <a href="/wiki/Z%C3%BCrich" title="Zürich">Zürich</a>.</p>
<p>Vienna has multiple road connections including motorways.</p>
<p>Vienna is served by <a href="/wiki/Vienna_International_Airport" title="Vienna International Airport">Vienna International Airport</a>, located 18 km (11 mi) southeast of the city centre next to the town of <a href="/wiki/Schwechat" title="Schwechat">Schwechat</a>. The airport handled approximately 22 million passengers in 2014. Following lengthy negotiations with surrounding communities, the airport will be expanded to increase its capacity by adding a third runway. The airport is currently undergoing a major expansion, including a new terminal building opened in 2012 to prepare for an expected increase in passengers.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="International_relations">International relations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Vienna&amp;action=edit&amp;section=41" title="Edit section: International relations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="International_organisations_in_Vienna">International organisations in Vienna</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Vienna&amp;action=edit&amp;section=42" title="Edit section: International organisations in Vienna">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Vereinte_Nationen_in_Wien.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="375" data-file-width="501" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/24/Vereinte_Nationen_in_Wien.jpg/220px-Vereinte_Nationen_in_Wien.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/24/Vereinte_Nationen_in_Wien.jpg/330px-Vereinte_Nationen_in_Wien.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/24/Vereinte_Nationen_in_Wien.jpg/440px-Vereinte_Nationen_in_Wien.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Vereinte_Nationen_in_Wien.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
UN complex in Vienna, with the Austria Center Vienna in front, taken from the <a href="/wiki/Donauturm" title="Donauturm">Danube Tower</a> in the nearby Donaupark before the extensive building work</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Donaucity_from_Danube_River_to_Northnorthwest_-_Vienna-.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3758" data-file-width="11210" height="74" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/19/Donaucity_from_Danube_River_to_Northnorthwest_-_Vienna-.jpg/220px-Donaucity_from_Danube_River_to_Northnorthwest_-_Vienna-.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/19/Donaucity_from_Danube_River_to_Northnorthwest_-_Vienna-.jpg/330px-Donaucity_from_Danube_River_to_Northnorthwest_-_Vienna-.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/19/Donaucity_from_Danube_River_to_Northnorthwest_-_Vienna-.jpg/440px-Donaucity_from_Danube_River_to_Northnorthwest_-_Vienna-.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Donaucity_from_Danube_River_to_Northnorthwest_-_Vienna-.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Many international organisations and offices are located in <a href="/wiki/Donaustadt" title="Donaustadt">Donaustadt</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Vienna is the seat of a number of United Nations offices and various international institutions and companies, including the <a href="/wiki/International_Atomic_Energy_Agency" title="International Atomic Energy Agency">International Atomic Energy Agency</a> (IAEA), the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Industrial_Development_Organization" title="United Nations Industrial Development Organization">United Nations Industrial Development Organization</a> (UNIDO), the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/UNODC" title="UNODC">United Nations Office on Drugs and Crime</a> (UNODC), the <a href="/wiki/OPEC" title="OPEC">Organization of Petroleum Exporting Countries</a> (OPEC), the <a href="/wiki/Comprehensive_Nuclear-Test-Ban_Treaty_Organization" title="Comprehensive Nuclear-Test-Ban Treaty Organization">Preparatory Commission for the Comprehensive Nuclear-Test-Ban Treaty Organization</a> (CTBTO), the <a href="/wiki/Organization_for_Security_and_Co-operation_in_Europe" title="Organization for Security and Co-operation in Europe">Organization for Security and Co-operation in Europe</a> (OSCE), the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Office_for_Outer_Space_Affairs" title="United Nations Office for Outer Space Affairs">United Nations Office for Outer Space Affairs</a> (UNOOSA) and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/European_Union_Agency_for_Fundamental_Rights" title="European Union Agency for Fundamental Rights">European Union Agency for Fundamental Rights</a> (FRA). Currently Vienna is the world's third "UN city", next to <a href="/wiki/New_York_City" title="New York City">New York</a>, <a href="/wiki/Geneva" title="Geneva">Geneva</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Nairobi" title="Nairobi">Nairobi</a>. Additionally, Vienna is the seat of the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Commission_on_International_Trade_Law" title="United Nations Commission on International Trade Law">United Nations Commission on International Trade Law</a>'s secretariat (<a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Commission_on_International_Trade_Law" title="United Nations Commission on International Trade Law">UNCITRAL</a>). In conjunction, the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Vienna" title="University of Vienna">University of Vienna</a> annually hosts the prestigious <a href="/wiki/Willem_C._Vis_Moot" title="Willem C. Vis Moot">Willem C. Vis Moot</a>, an international commercial arbitration competition for students of law from around the world.</p>
<p>Various special diplomatic meetings have been held in Vienna in the latter half of the 20th century, resulting in various documents bearing the name <a class="mw-redirect mw-disambig" href="/wiki/Vienna_Convention_(disambiguation)" title="Vienna Convention (disambiguation)">Vienna Convention</a> or Vienna Document. Among the more important documents negotiated in Vienna are the 1969 <a href="/wiki/Vienna_Convention_on_the_Law_of_Treaties" title="Vienna Convention on the Law of Treaties">Vienna Convention on the Law of Treaties</a>, as well as the 1990 <a href="/wiki/Treaty_on_Conventional_Armed_Forces_in_Europe" title="Treaty on Conventional Armed Forces in Europe">Treaty on Conventional Armed Forces in Europe</a>. Vienna also hosted the negotiations leading to the 2015 <a href="/wiki/Joint_Comprehensive_Plan_of_Action" title="Joint Comprehensive Plan of Action">Joint Comprehensive Plan of Action</a> on Iran's nuclear program as well as the <a href="/wiki/Vienna_peace_talks_for_Syria" title="Vienna peace talks for Syria">Vienna peace talks for Syria</a>.</p>
<p>Vienna also headquartered the <a href="/wiki/International_Taekwon-Do_Federation" title="International Taekwon-Do Federation">International Taekwon-Do Federation</a> (ITF).</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Charitable_organisations_in_Vienna">Charitable organisations in Vienna</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Vienna&amp;action=edit&amp;section=43" title="Edit section: Charitable organisations in Vienna">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Alongside international and intergovernmental organisations, there are dozens of charitable organisations based in Vienna.. One such organisation is the network of <a href="/wiki/SOS_Children%27s_Villages" title="SOS Children's Villages">SOS Children's Villages</a>, founded by <a href="/wiki/Hermann_Gmeiner" title="Hermann Gmeiner">Hermann Gmeiner</a> in 1949. Today, SOS Children's Villages are active in 132 countries and territories worldwide. Others include <a href="/wiki/Help_Afghan_School_Children_Organization" title="Help Afghan School Children Organization">HASCO</a>.</p>
<p>Another extremely popular international event is the annual <a href="/wiki/Life_Ball" title="Life Ball">Life Ball</a>, which supports people with <a href="/wiki/HIV" title="HIV">HIV</a> or <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/AIDS" title="AIDS">AIDS</a>. Guests such as <a href="/wiki/Bill_Clinton" title="Bill Clinton">Bill Clinton</a> and <a href="/wiki/Whoopi_Goldberg" title="Whoopi Goldberg">Whoopi Goldberg</a> were recent attendees.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="International_City_Cooperations">International City Cooperations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Vienna&amp;action=edit&amp;section=44" title="Edit section: International City Cooperations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The general policy of the City of Vienna is not to sign any <a href="/wiki/Twin_towns_and_sister_cities" title="Twin towns and sister cities">twin or sister city</a> agreements with other cities. Instead Vienna has only cooperation agreements in which specific cooperation areas are defined.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-115"><a href="#cite_note-115">[115]</a></sup></p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="District_to_district_partnerships">District to district partnerships</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Vienna&amp;action=edit&amp;section=45" title="Edit section: District to district partnerships">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In addition, individual Viennese districts have international partnerships all over the world. A detailed list can be found on the following webpage of the <a class="external text" href="https://www.wien.gv.at/english/politics/international/networks/district-partnerships.html" rel="nofollow">City of Vienna.</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-116"><a href="#cite_note-116">[116]</a></sup></p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Further_reading">Further reading</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Vienna&amp;action=edit&amp;section=48" title="Edit section: Further reading">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/Martina_Pippal" title="Martina Pippal">Pippal, M.</a>: <i>A short History of Art in Vienna</i>, Munich: C.H. Beck 2000, <a class="internal mw-magiclink-isbn" href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/9783406467899">ISBN 978-3-406-46789-9</a>, provides a concise overview.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Robert_von_Dassanowsky" title="Robert von Dassanowsky">Dassanowsky, Robert</a> ed, : "World Film Locations: Vienna", London: Intellect/Chicago: U of Chicago Press, 2012, <a class="internal mw-magiclink-isbn" href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/9781841505695">ISBN 978-1-84150-569-5</a>. International films about Vienna or Austria shot on location throughout cinema history.</li>
</ul>
